<pr_description>
I18nProvider ignores lang after upgrade from 3.0.0 to 3.0.2
After upgrading next-translate from 3.0.0 to 3.0.2 I can no longer change my app's language. Regardless of which language I pass to I18nProvider, the app always renders using the default language. Rolling back to 3.0.0 restores expected behavior.

Environment:
next: 16.1.6 (webpack)
react: 19.2.4
next-translate-plugin: 2.6.2 (also tried 3.0.2)
next-translate: 3.0.2 (next-translate-plugin peer dependecy)

Reproduction:

```ts
export default function App({ Component, pageProps }: AppProps) {
  const [lang, setLang] = useState('en')

  return (
    <I18nProvider key={lang} lang={lang}>
      <DynamicNamespaces namespaces={['common']}>
        <Component {...pageProps} onLanguageChange={setLang} />
      </DynamicNamespaces>
    </I18nProvider>
  )
}
```

```ts
export default function Home({ onLanguageChange }: HomeProps) {
  const { t, lang } = useTranslation('common')
  return (
    <div className="h-svh flex flex-col items-center justify-center">
      <LanguageSelector onLanguageChange={onLanguageChange} />
      <strong className="mt-4 text-2xl">Current Language:</strong>{' '}
      {t('languageName')} ({lang})
    </div>
  )
}
```
```ts
export const LanguageSelector: React.FC<LanguageSelectorProps> = ({
  onLanguageChange,
}) => {
  const { t, lang } = useTranslation('common')

  const LANGUAGES = [
  { code: 'en', name: 'English' },
  { code: 'es', name: 'Español' },
  { code: 'fr', name: 'Français' },
  { code: 'pt', name: 'Português' },
]

  const handleLanguageChange = (e: React.ChangeEvent<HTMLSelectElement>) => {
    const newLang = e.target.value
    if (onLanguageChange) {
      onLanguageChange(newLang)
    }
  }

  return (
    <div>
      <label htmlFor="language-select">
        {t('selectLabel')}
      </label>
      <select
        id="language-select"
        value={lang}
        onChange={handleLanguageChange}
      >
        {LANGUAGES.map((language) => (
          <option key={language.code} value={language.code}>
            {language.name}
          </option>
        ))}
      </select>
    </div>
  )
}
```
Or clone this project: https://github.com/dmg-vicente/next-language-bug (uses 3.0.0 by default)

     9	
    10	export default function I18nProvider({
    11	  lang: lng,
    12	  namespaces = {},
    13	  children,
    14	  config: newConfig = {},
    15	}: I18nProviderProps) {
    16	  const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
    17	  const { locale, defaultLocale } = useRouter() || {}
    18	  const internal = useContext(InternalContext)
    19	  const allNamespaces: Record<string, I18nDictionary> = {
    20	    ...initialBrowserNamespaces(),
    21	    ...internal.ns,
    22	    ...namespaces,
    23	  }
    24	  const lang = lng || parentLang || locale || defaultLocale || ''
    25	  const config = { ...internal.config, ...newConfig }
    26	  const localesToIgnore = config.localesToIgnore || ['default']
    27	  const ignoreLang = !lang || localesToIgnore.includes(lang)
    28	  const pluralRules = new Intl.PluralRules(ignoreLang ? undefined : lang)
    29	  const t = transCore({ config, allNamespaces, pluralRules, lang })
    30

    33	      <InternalContext.Provider value={{ ns: allNamespaces, config }}>
    34	        {children}
    35	      </InternalContext.Provider>
    36	    </I18nContext.Provider>
    37	  )
    38	}

     2	  I18nConfig,
     3	  I18nDictionary,
     4	  LoaderConfig,
     5	  LoggerProps,
     6	  TranslationQuery,
     7	} from '.'
     8	import { Translate } from './index'
     9	
    10	function splitNsKey(key: string, nsSeparator: string | false) {
    11	  if (!nsSeparator) return { i18nKey: key }
    12	  const i = key.indexOf(nsSeparator)
    13	  if (i < 0) return { i18nKey: key }
    14	  return {
    15	    namespace: key.slice(0, i),
    16	    i18nKey: key.slice(i + nsSeparator.length),
    17	  }
    18	}
    19	
    20	export default function transCore({
    21	  config,
    22	  allNamespaces,
    23	  pluralRules,
    24	  lang,
    25	}: {
    26	  config: LoaderConfig
    27	  allNamespaces: Record<string, I18nDictionary>
    28	  pluralRules: Intl.PluralRules
    29	  lang: string | undefined
    30	}): Translate {
    31	  const {
    32	    logger = missingKeyLogger,
    33	    // An optional parameter allowEmptyStrings - true as default.
    34	    // If allowEmptyStrings parameter is marked as false,
    35	    // it should log an error when an empty string is attempted to be translated
    36	    // and return the namespace and key as result of the translation.
    37	    allowEmptyStrings = true,
    38	  } = config
    39	
    40	  const interpolateUnknown = (
    41	    value: unknown,
    42	    query?: TranslationQuery | null
    43	  ): typeof value => {
    44	    if (Array.isArray(value)) {
    45	      return value.map((val) => interpolateUnknown(val, query))
    46	    }
    47	    if (value instanceof Object) {
    48	      return objectInterpolation({
    49	        obj: value as Record<string, unknown>,
    50	        query,
    51	        config,
    52	        lang,
    53	      })
    54	    }
    55	    return interpolation({ text: value as string, query, config, lang })
    56	  }
    57	
    58	  const t: Translate = (key = '', query, options) => {
    59	    const k = Array.isArray(key) ? key[0] : key
    60	    const { nsSeparator = ':', loggerEnvironment = 'browser' } = config
    61	
    62	    const { i18nKey, namespace = options?.ns ?? config.defaultNS } = splitNsKey(
    63	      k,
    64	      nsSeparator
    65	    )
    66	
    67	    const dic = (namespace && allNamespaces[namespace]) || {}
    68	    const keyWithPlural = plural(
    69	      pluralRules,
    70	      dic,
    71	      i18nKey,
    72	      config,
    73	      query,
    74	      options
    75	    )
    76	    const dicValue = getDicValue(dic, keyWithPlural, config, options)
    77	    const value =
    78	      typeof dicValue === 'object'
    79	        ? JSON.parse(JSON.stringify(dicValue))
    80	        : dicValue
    81	
    82	    const empty =
    83	      typeof value === 'undefined' ||
    84	      (typeof value === 'object' && !Object.keys(value).length) ||
    85	      (value === '' && !allowEmptyStrings)
    86	
    87	    const fallbacks =
    88	      typeof options?.fallback === 'string'
    89	        ? [options.fallback]
    90	        : options?.fallback || []
    91	
    92	    if (
    93	      empty &&
    94	      (loggerEnvironment === 'both' ||
    95	        loggerEnvironment ===
    96	          (typeof window === 'undefined' ? 'node' : 'browser'))
    97	    ) {
    98	      logger({ namespace, i18nKey })
    99	    }
   100	
   101	    // Fallbacks
   102	    if (empty && Array.isArray(fallbacks) && fallbacks.length) {
   103	      const [firstFallback, ...restFallbacks] = fallbacks
   104	      if (typeof firstFallback === 'string') {
   105	        return t(firstFallback, query, { ...options, fallback: restFallbacks })
   106	      }
   107	    }
   108	
   109	    if (
   110	      empty &&
   111	      options &&
   112	      // options.default could be a nullish value so check that the property exists
   113	      options.hasOwnProperty('default') &&
   114	      !fallbacks?.length
   115	    ) {
   116	      // if options.default is falsey there's no reason to do interpolation
   117	      return options.default
   118	        ? interpolateUnknown(options.default, query)
   119	        : options.default
   120	    }
   121	
   122	    // no need to try interpolation
   123	    if (empty) {
   124	      return k
   125	    }
   126	
   127	    // this can return an empty string if either value was already empty
   128	    // or it contained only an interpolation (e.g. "{{name}}") and the query param was empty
   129	    return interpolateUnknown(value, query)
   130	  }
   131	
   132	  return t
   133	}
   134	
   135	/**
   136	 * Get value from key (allow nested keys as parent.children)
   137	 */
   138	function getDicValue(
   139	  dic: I18nDictionary,
   140	  key: string = '',
   141	  config: I18nConfig,
   142	  options: { returnObjects?: boolean; fallback?: string | string[] } = {
   143	    returnObjects: false,
   144	  }
   145	): unknown | undefined {
   146	  const { keySeparator = '.' } = config || {}
   147	  const keyParts = keySeparator ? key.split(keySeparator) : [key]
   148	
   149	  if (key === keySeparator && options.returnObjects) return dic
   150	
   151	  const value: string | object = keyParts.reduce(
   152	    (val: I18nDictionary | string, key: string) => {
   153	      if (typeof val === 'string') {
   154	        return {}
   155	      }
   156	
   157	      const res = val[key as keyof typeof val]
   158	
   159	      // pass all truthy values or (empty) strings
   160	      return res || (typeof res === 'string' ? res : {})
   161	    },
   162	    dic
   163	  )
   164	
   165	  if (
   166	    typeof value === 'string' ||
   167	    ((value as unknown) instanceof Object &&
   168	      options.returnObjects &&
   169	      Object.keys(value).length > 0)
   170	  ) {
   171	    return value
   172	  }
   173	
   174	  if (Array.isArray(value) && options.returnObjects) return value
   175	  return undefined
   176	}
   177	
   178	/**
   179	 * Control plural keys depending the {{count}} variable
   180	 */
   181	function plural(
   182	  pluralRules: Intl.PluralRules,
   183	  dic: I18nDictionary,
   184	  key: string,
   185	  config: I18nConfig,
   186	  query?: TranslationQuery | null,
   187	  options?: {
   188	    returnObjects?: boolean
   189	    fallback?: string | string[]
   190	  }
   191	): string {
   192	  if (!query || typeof query.count !== 'number') return key
   193	
   194	  const numKey = `${key}_${query.count}`
   195	  if (getDicValue(dic, numKey, config, options) !== undefined) return numKey
   196	
   197	  const pluralKey = `${key}_${pluralRules.select(query.count)}`
   198	  if (getDicValue(dic, pluralKey, config, options) !== undefined) {
   199	    return pluralKey
   200	  }
   201	
   202	  const nestedNumKey = `${key}.${query.count}`
   203	  if (getDicValue(dic, nestedNumKey, config, options) !== undefined)
   204	    return nestedNumKey
   205	
   206	  const nestedKey = `${key}.${pluralRules.select(query.count)}`
   207	  if (getDicValue(dic, nestedKey, config, options) !== undefined)
   208	    return nestedKey
   209	
   210	  return key
   211	}
   212	
   213	/**
   214	 * Replace {{variables}} to query values
   215	 */
   216	function interpolation({
   217	  text,
   218	  query,
   219	  config,
   220	  lang,
   221	}: {
   222	  text?: string
   223	  query?: TranslationQuery | null
   224	  config: I18nConfig
   225	  lang?: string | undefined
   226	}): string {
   227	  if (!text || !query) return text || ''
   228	
   229	  const escapeRegex = (str: string) =>
   230	    str.replace(/[-\/\\^$*+?.()|[\]{}]/g, '\\$&')
   231	  const {
   232	    format = null,
   233	    prefix = '{{',
   234	    suffix = '}}',
   235	  } = config.interpolation || {}
   236	
   237	  const regexEnd =
   238	    suffix === '' ? '' : `(?:[\\s,]+([\\w-]*))?\\s*${escapeRegex(suffix)}`
   239	  return Object.keys(query).reduce((all, varKey) => {
   240	    const regex = new RegExp(
   241	      `${escapeRegex(prefix)}\\s*${varKey}${regexEnd}`,
   242	      'gm'
   243	    )
   244	    // $1 is the first match group
   245	    return all.replace(regex, (_match, $1) => {
   246	      // $1 undefined can mean either no formatting requested: "{{name}}"
   247	      // or no format name given: "{{name, }}" -> ignore
   248	      return $1 && format
   249	        ? (format(query[varKey], $1, lang) as string)
   250	        : (query[varKey] as string)
   251	    })
   252	  }, text)
   253	}
   254	
   255	function objectInterpolation({
   256	  obj,
   257	  query,
   258	  config,
   259	  lang,
   260	}: {
   261	  obj: Record<string, string | unknown>
   262	  query?: TranslationQuery | null
   263	  config: I18nConfig
   264	  lang?: string
   265	}): any {
   266	  if (!query || Object.keys(query).length === 0) return obj
   267	  Object.keys(obj).forEach((key) => {
   268	    if (obj[key] instanceof Object)
   269	      objectInterpolation({
   270	        obj: obj[key] as Record<string, string | unknown>,
   271	        query,
   272	        config,
   273	        lang,
   274	      })
   275	    if (typeof obj[key] === 'string')
   276	      obj[key] = interpolation({
   277	        text: obj[key] as string,
   278	        query,
   279	        config,
   280	        lang,
   281	      })
   282	  })
   283	
   284	  return obj
   285	}
   286	
   287	function missingKeyLogger({ namespace, i18nKey }: LoggerProps): void {
   288	  if (process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production') return
   289	
   290	  // This means that instead of "ns:value", "value" has been misspelled (without namespace)
   291	  if (!namespace) {
   292	    console.warn(
   293	      `[next-translate] The text "${i18nKey}" has no namespace in front of it.`
   294	    )
   295	    return
   296	  }
   297	  console.warn(
   298	    `[next-translate] "${namespace}:${i18nKey}" is missing in current namespace configuration. Try adding "${i18nKey}" to the namespace "${namespace}".`
   299	  )
   300	}

   147	//////// For type safety (next-translate.d.ts):  ///////////
   148	/*
   149	 *
   150	 * import type { Paths, I18n, Translate } from "next-translate";
   151	 *
   152	 * export interface TranslationsKeys {
   153	 *   common: Paths<typeof import("./locales/en/common.json")>;
   154	 *   home: Paths<typeof import("./locales/en/home.json")>;
   155	 * }
   156	 *
   157	 * export interface TypeSafeTranslate<Namespace extends keyof TranslationsKeys>
   158	 *   extends Omit<I18n, "t"> {
   159	 *   t: {
   160	 *     (key: TranslationsKeys[Namespace], ...rest: Tail<Parameters<Translate>>): string;
   161	 *     <T extends string>(template: TemplateStringsArray): string;
   162	 *   };
   163	 * }
   164	 *
   165	 * declare module "next-translate/useTranslation" {
   166	 *   export default function useTranslation<
   167	 *     Namespace extends keyof TranslationsKeys,
   168	 *   >(namespace: Namespace): TypeSafeTranslate<Namespace>;
   169	 * }
   170	 */
   171	
   172	type RemovePlural<Key extends string> = Key extends `${infer Prefix}${
   173	  | '_zero'
   174	  | '_one'
   175	  | '_two'
   176	  | '_few'
   177	  | '_many'
   178	  | '_other'
   179	  | `_${number}`}`
   180	  ? Prefix
   181	  : Key
   182	
   183	type Join<S1, S2> = S1 extends string
   184	  ? S2 extends string
   185	    ? `${S1}.${S2}`
   186	    : never
   187	  : never
   188	
   189	// @ts-ignore
   190	export type Paths<T> = RemovePlural<
   191	  // @ts-ignore
   192	  {
   193	    // @ts-ignore
   194	    [K in Extract<keyof T, string>]: T[K] extends Record<string, unknown>
   195	      ? Join<K, Paths<T[K]>>
   196	      : K
   197	  }[Extract<keyof T, string>]
   198	>
   199	
   200	// TODO: Remove this in future versions > 2.0.0
   201	function nextTranslate(nextConfig: NextConfig = {}): NextConfig {
   202	  console.log(`
   203	    #########################################################################
   204	    #                                                                       #
   205	    #   next-translate plugin in 2.0.0 is replaced by                       #
   206	    #   next-translate-plugin package:                                      #
   207	    #                                                                       #
   208	    #   > yarn add next-translate-plugin -D                                 #
   209	    #   or:                                                                 #
   210	    #   > npm install next-translate-plugin --save-dev                      #
   211	    #                                                                       #
   212	    #   replace in next.config.js file:                                     #
   213	    #    const nextTranslate = require('next-translate')                    #
   214	    #   to:                                                                 #
   215	    #    const nextTranslate = require('next-translate-plugin')             #
   216	    #                                                                       #
   217	    #########################################################################
   218	  `)
   219	  return nextConfig
   220	}
   221	
   222	module.exports = nextTranslate
   223	export default nextTranslate
   224

The key issue is in `I18nProvider.tsx` line 16:
```tsx
const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
```

This calls `useTranslation()` which reads from `I18nContext`. But the issue is that the `useTranslation` hook uses `useMemo` with `[ctx, defaultNS]` as dependencies. The `ctx` is the object `{ lang, t }`. When `lang` changes but `t` function reference stays the same (or vice versa), the `useMemo` may not update.

But wait, let me look more carefully. The issue in `I18nProvider`:

```tsx
const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
```

This reads from the context — but the `I18nProvider` itself is what provides the context. So when a nested `I18nProvider` reads from context, it gets the parent's context. But there's a subtlety: the first time it renders, `useTranslation()` returns the default context `{ t: ..., lang: '' }`.

2026-05-30 07:49:34,556 - INFO - swea-agent-aralroca__next-translate-1259 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now let me think about this issue. The PR description says that after upgrading from 3.0.0 to 3.0.2, `I18nProvider` ignores `lang`. 

Let me look at the `useTranslation` function more carefully:

```tsx
function useTranslationInPages(defaultNS?: string): I18n {
  const ctx = useContext(I18nContext)
  return useMemo(
    () => ({
      ...ctx,
      t: wrapTWithDefaultNs(ctx.t, defaultNS),
    }),
    [ctx, defaultNS]
  )
}
```

The issue is `[ctx, defaultNS]` — `ctx` is an object `{ lang, t }` from context. When React compares `ctx` in the dependency array, it uses reference equality. Since the context provider creates a new `{ lang, t }` object every time it renders, `ctx` should be a new reference each time.

But wait, let me look at `I18nProvider` again:

```tsx
const t = transCore({ config, allNamespaces, pluralRules, lang })

return (
  <I18nContext.Provider value={{ lang, t }}>
    ...
  </I18nContext.Provider>
)
```

The provider value is `{ lang, t }` — a new object each render. So `ctx` in `useTranslation` would be a new reference each time the provider renders, triggering the `useMemo` to recalculate.

Now let me think about the scenario in the PR:

```tsx
export default function App({ Component, pageProps }: AppProps) {
  const [lang, setLang] = useState('en')

  return (
    <I18nProvider key={lang} lang={lang}>
      <DynamicNamespaces namespaces={['common']}>
        <Component {...pageProps} onLanguageChange={setLang} />
      </DynamicNamespaces>
    </I18nProvider>
  )
}
```

The user uses `key={lang}` to force remount when lang changes. This should work...

But wait, there's another issue. Let me look at `I18nProvider` again:

```tsx
const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
```

If `lng` is provided (which it is), then `lang = lng`. So `parentLang` shouldn't matter. But the issue is about `I18nProvider` ignoring lang.

Let me check the lib (built) versions to understand what might have changed.

2026-05-30 07:50:14,631 - INFO - swea-agent-aralroca__next-translate-1259 - 💭 THOUGHT
All tests pass. Now let me write a reproduction script to confirm the issue described in the PR.

The issue is: when changing the `lang` prop on `I18nProvider`, the language doesn't actually change. Let me create a test to reproduce this:



🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/repro.test.js << 'EOF'
import React, { useState } from 'react'
import { render, cleanup, fireEvent, act } from '@testing-library/react'
import I18nProvider from './src/I18nProvider'
import useTranslation from './src/useTranslation'

describe('I18nProvider lang change', () => {
  afterEach(cleanup)

  test('should update language when lang prop changes', () => {
    const Inner = () => {
      const { t, lang } = useTranslation()
      return <div>{lang}: {t('common:hello')}</div>
    }

    const App = () => {
      const [lang, setLang] = useState('en')
      return (
        <div>
          <button onClick={() => setLang('es')}>Change to ES</button>
          <I18nProvider key={lang} lang={lang} namespaces={{
            en: { common: { hello: 'Hello' } },
            es: { common: { hello: 'Hola' } },
          }}>
            <Inner />
          </I18nProvider>
        </div>
      )
    }

    const { container } = render(<App />)
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('en: Hello')
    
    // Change language
    fireEvent.click(container.querySelector('button'))
    
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('es: Hola')
  })
  
  test('should update language when lang prop changes without key (re-render)', () => {
    const namespaces = {
      common: {
        hello_en: 'Hello',
        hello_es: 'Hola',
      }
    }
    
    let currentLang = 'en'
    let setLang
    
    const Inner = () => {
      const { t, lang } = useTranslation()
      return <div>{lang}: {t('common:hello_' + lang)}</div>
    }

    const App = () => {
      const [lang, _setLang] = useState('en')
      setLang = _setLang
      currentLang = lang
      return (
        <div>
          <I18nProvider lang={lang} namespaces={namespaces}>
            <Inner />
          </I18nProvider>
        </div>
      )
    }

    const { container } = render(<App />)
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('en: Hello')
    
    // Change language
    act(() => setLang('es'))
    
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('es: Hola')
  })
})
EOF
npx jest --env=jsdom /tmp/repro.test.js 2>&1

import React, { useState } from 'react'
import { render, cleanup, fireEvent, act } from '@testing-library/react'
import I18nProvider from '../src/I18nProvider'
import useTranslation from '../src/useTranslation'

describe('I18nProvider lang change', () => {
  afterEach(cleanup)

  test('should update language when lang prop changes', () => {
    const Inner = () => {
      const { t, lang } = useTranslation()
      return <div>{lang}: {t('common:hello')}</div>
    }

    const App = () => {
      const [lang, setLang] = useState('en')
      return (
        <div>
          <button onClick={() => setLang('es')}>Change to ES</button>
          <I18nProvider key={lang} lang={lang} namespaces={{
            common: { hello: lang === 'en' ? 'Hello' : 'Hola' },
          }}>
            <Inner />
          </I18nProvider>
        </div>
      )
    }

    const { container } = render(<App />)
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('en: Hello')
    
    // Change language
    fireEvent.click(container.querySelector('button'))
    
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('es: Hola')
  })
  
  test('should update language when lang prop changes without key (re-render)', () => {
    const namespaces = {
      common: {
        hello_en: 'Hello',
        hello_es: 'Hola',
      }
    }
    
    let setLang
    
    const Inner = () => {
      const { t, lang } = useTranslation()
      return <div>{lang}: {t('common:hello_' + lang)}</div>
    }

    const App = () => {
      const [lang, _setLang] = useState('en')
      setLang = _setLang
      return (
        <div>
          <I18nProvider lang={lang} namespaces={namespaces}>
            <Inner />
          </I18nProvider>
        </div>
      )
    }

    const { container } = render(<App />)
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('en: Hello')
    
    // Change language
    act(() => setLang('es'))
    
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('es: Hola')
  })
})
EOF

```tsx
function useTranslationInPages(defaultNS?: string): I18n {
  const ctx = useContext(I18nContext)
  return useMemo(
    () => ({
      ...ctx,
      t: wrapTWithDefaultNs(ctx.t, defaultNS),
    }),
    [ctx, defaultNS]
  )

```

```tsx
  ...
```

Let me think about this more carefully. The PR says `I18nProvider` ignores `lang`. Let me look at the line:

```tsx
const lang = lng || parentLang || locale || defaultLocale || ''
```

If `lng` is provided, it should be used. But there's an issue: in the PR description, the user passes `key={lang}` to `I18nProvider`. When `lang` changes, the component remounts because of the key change. So that should work...

But wait, let me look at the `useTranslation` again. The `useTranslationInPages` function:

```tsx
function useTranslationInPages(defaultNS?: string): I18n {
  const ctx = useContext(I18nContext)
  return useMemo(
    () => ({
      ...ctx,
      t: wrapTWithDefaultNs(ctx.t, defaultNS),
    }),
    [ctx, defaultNS]
  )
}
```

Notice the dependency `[ctx, defaultNS]`. `ctx` is the value from context, which is `{ lang, t }`. This object is created new each render by `I18nProvider`. So it should work.

But hold on - what about the case where `useTranslation()` is called INSIDE the `I18nProvider`? Look at line 16 of `I18nProvider.tsx`:

```tsx
const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
```

This is called before the provider returns the new context. So it reads from the parent context. Now, `useTranslation` uses `useMemo` with `[ctx, defaultNS]`. 

Let me check if there's an issue with how `ctx` is compared. In React, `useMemo` uses `Object.is` for comparison. An object `{ lang: '', t: ... }` is compared by reference. If the parent `I18nProvider` creates a new `{ lang, t }` each time, then the reference changes and `useMemo` recalculates.

But what if the parent is the default context (when there's no parent `I18nProvider`)? The default context is defined in `context.tsx`:

```tsx
context = React.createContext<I18n>({
  t: (k) => (Array.isArray(k) ? k[0] : k),
  lang: '',
})
```

This default value is a stable object. So if there's no parent `I18nProvider`, `ctx` is always the same reference. But this shouldn't matter because `lng` is provided and takes precedence.

Let me think about this differently. Let me look at what could have changed between 3.0.0 and 3.0.2 that would cause the `lang` to be ignored. 

Maybe the issue is not in the `lang` variable itself but in how the `t` function is created. If `t` is stable (same reference) when `lang` changes, then React components using `useTranslation` might not re-render because `useMemo` depends on `ctx` which contains both `lang` and `t`. But if `t` is a new function each time, `ctx` will be a new reference.

Wait, let me check the `transCore` function more carefully. When `lang` changes, `transCore` returns a new function. But what if `lang` is the same as before? Let's trace through the code:

1. User changes `lang` from 'en' to 'es'
2. `I18nProvider` receives new `lang` prop
3. `lang = lng || parentLang || locale || defaultLocale || ''` → 'es'
4. `t = transCore({ config, allNamespaces, pluralRules, lang })` → new function
5. Provider value is `{ lang: 'es', t }` → new object

This should work...

Let me look at the `getT` function to see if there's another path:

Wait, I see something interesting. Let me look at the `I18nProvider` again:

```tsx
const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
```

And `useTranslation`:

```tsx
function useTranslationInPages(defaultNS?: string): I18n {
  const ctx = useContext(I18nContext)
  return useMemo(
    () => ({
      ...ctx,
      t: wrapTWithDefaultNs(ctx.t, defaultNS),
    }),
    [ctx, defaultNS]
  )
}
```

Now, what's the issue? The `ctx` is `{ lang, t }`. The `t` function is created by `transCore`. But look at the `wrapTWithDefaultNs`:

```tsx
export default function wrapTWithDefaultNs(
  oldT: Translate,
  ns?: string
): Translate {
  if (typeof ns !== 'string') return oldT

  // Use default namespace if namespace is missing
  const t: Translate = (key, query, options) => {
    return oldT(key, query, { ns, ...options })
  }

  return t
}
```

When `ns` is not provided (which is the case for `I18nProvider` calling `useTranslation()`), `wrapTWithDefaultNs` returns the same `oldT` reference. So `ctx.t` from the parent context is passed through unchanged.

But wait - the issue might be something else. Let me look at the `I18nProvider` more carefully:

```tsx
const t = transCore({ config, allNamespaces, pluralRules, lang })

return (
  <I18nContext.Provider value={{ lang, t }}>
    <InternalContext.Provider value={{ ns: allNamespaces, config }}>
      {children}
    </InternalContext.Provider>
  </I18nContext.Provider>
)
```

Notice that `config` and `allNamespaces` are merged from both `internal` context and props. The `InternalContext` is used by nested `I18nProvider`s to access parent namespaces and config.

Now, let me think about what happens when the user uses the pattern from the PR description:

```tsx
export default function App({ Component, pageProps }: AppProps) {
  const [lang, setLang] = useState('en')

  return (
    <I18nProvider key={lang} lang={lang}>
      <DynamicNamespaces namespaces={['common']}>
        <Component {...pageProps} onLanguageChange={setLang} />
      </DynamicNamespaces>
    </I18nProvider>
  )
}
```

The `I18nProvider` gets `key={lang}` which forces remount when lang changes. So the component remounts completely. Inside it, `DynamicNamespaces` loads namespaces and renders ANOTHER `I18nProvider`:

```tsx
return (
  <I18nProvider
    lang={lang}
    namespaces={...}
  >
    {children}
  </I18nProvider>
)
```

So there are nested `I18nProvider`s. The outer one has `key={lang}` and `lang={lang}`. The inner one (from `DynamicNamespaces`) has `lang={lang}` from `useTranslation()` which reads from the outer provider.

Hmm, wait. The `DynamicNamespaces` component uses `useTranslation()` to get the current `lang`, and passes it to its own `I18nProvider`. This should work.

But wait - there's a subtle bug I just noticed. Look at `I18nProvider.tsx` line 21:

```tsx
const allNamespaces: Record<string, I18nDictionary> = {

  ...internal.ns,
  ...namespaces,
}
```

And line 25:

```tsx
const config = { ...internal.config, ...newConfig }
```

Notice that the `initialBrowserNamespaces()` comes FIRST, then `internal.ns`, then `namespaces`. So `namespaces` (the prop) has highest priority. But `initialBrowserNamespaces()` reads from `window.__NEXT_DATA__?.props?.__namespaces`, which could be the initial SSR namespaces. If those are set, they might override things. But this is probably not the issue.

Now  let me think about this differently. The user's reproduction code uses `DynamicNamespaces`. Let me look at `DynamicNamespaces` more carefully.

```tsx
export default function DynamicNamespaces({
  dynamic,
  namespaces = [],
  fallback,
  children,
}: DynamicNamespacesProps): any {
  const config = useContext(InternalContext).config as I18nConfig
  const { lang } = useTranslation()
  const [loaded, setLoaded] = useState(false)
  const [pageNs, setPageNs] = useState<I18nDictionary[]>([])
  const loadLocale =
    dynamic || config.loadLocaleFrom || (() => Promise.resolve({}))

  async function loadNamespaces() {
    if (typeof loadLocale !== 'function') return

    const pageNamespaces = await Promise.all(
      namespaces.map((ns) => loadLocale(lang, ns))
    )
    setPageNs(pageNamespaces)
    setLoaded(true)
  }

  useEffect(() => {
    loadNamespaces()
  }, [namespaces.join()])
  ...
```

The `useEffect` depends on `[namespaces.join()]`. When `lang` changes but the `namespaces` array stays the same (`['common']`), the effect does NOT re-run. So the namespaces are NOT reloaded when the language changes!

But wait, the user uses `key={lang}` on the outer `I18nProvider`, which forces remount of the whole tree including `DynamicNamespaces`. So when the outer `I18nProvider` remounts, `DynamicNamespaces` remounts fresh and loads the namespaces again.

But here's a subtle issue: when `DynamicNamespaces` remounts, it calls `loadNamespaces()` which uses `lang` from `useTranslation()`. At that point, what is `lang`? It comes from the outer `I18nProvider` which just rendered with the new `lang` prop. But wait...

`I18nProvider` calls `useTranslation()` to get `parentLang`. But when `key={lang}` changes, the component unmounts and remounts. When it mounts, it reads from the parent context. If there's no parent `I18nProvider`, it gets the default context `{ lang: '', t: ... }`. Then `lang = lng || parentLang || locale || defaultLocale || ''`. Since `lng` is provided ('es'), `lang` = 'es'. Good.

Then `DynamicNamespaces` mounts inside it. `DynamicNamespaces` calls `useTranslation()` which reads from the just-created context. It should get `lang: 'es'`. Then it calls `loadLocale('es', 'common')` which should return the correct translations.

So this should work. Let me write a more accurate reproduction test:



🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && cat > __tests__/repro2.test.js << 'EOF'
import React, { useState, useCallback } from 'react'
import { render, cleanup, fireEvent, act } from '@testing-library/react'
import I18nProvider from '../src/I18nProvider'
import useTranslation from '../src/useTranslation'

// Simulate the pattern from the PR description
describe('PR reproduction', () => {
  afterEach(cleanup)

  test('DynamicNamespaces-like pattern with lang change', () => {
    // This simulates the PR description's App component
    const namespacesData = {
      en: { common: { hello: 'Hello', languageName: 'English' } },
      es: { common: { hello: 'Hola', languageName: 'Español' } },
      fr: { common: { hello: 'Bonjour', languageName: 'Français' } },
    }
    
    const Inner = () => {
      const { t, lang } = useTranslation()
      return <div>{lang}:{t('common:hello')}</div>
    }
    
    const DynamicNamespaces = ({ namespaces, children }) => {
      const { lang } = useTranslation()
      // Simulate loading namespaces
      const ns = namespaces.reduce((obj, nsName) => {
        obj[nsName] = namespacesData[lang]?.[nsName] || {}
        return obj
      }, {})
      
      return (
        <I18nProvider lang={lang} namespaces={ns}>
          {children}
        </I18nProvider>
      )
    }

    const App = () => {
      const [lang, setLang] = useState('en')
      return (
        <div>
          <button onClick={() => setLang('es')}>ES</button>
          <button onClick={() => setLang('fr')}>FR</button>
          <I18nProvider key={lang} lang={lang} namespaces={namespacesData[lang]}>
            <DynamicNamespaces namespaces={['common']}>
              <Inner />
            </DynamicNamespaces>
          </I18nProvider>
        </div>
      )
    }

    const { container } = render(<App />)
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('en:Hello')
    
    // Change to ES
    fireEvent.click(container.querySelectorAll('button')[0])
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('es:Hola')
    
    // Change to FR
    fireEvent.click(container.querySelectorAll('button')[1])
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('fr:Bonjour')
  })
})
EOF

```tsx
function useTranslationInPages(defaultNS?: string): I18n {
  const ctx = useContext(I18nContext)
  return useMemo(
    () => ({
      ...ctx,
      t: wrapTWithDefaultNs(ctx.t, defaultNS),
    }),
    [ctx, defaultNS]
  )

```

And `I18nProvider`:

```tsx
const t = transCore({ config, allNamespaces, pluralRules, lang })

return (
  <I18nContext.Provider value={{ lang, t }}>
    ...
  </I18nContext.Provider>
)
```

The provider creates `{ lang, t }` as value. In React, when a context provider re-renders, it provides a new value. So `ctx` in `useTranslation` should be a new reference.

But wait - there's a subtle issue with `useMemo`. The dependency array is `[ctx, defaultNS]`. If `ctx` is a new object each time, `useMemo` recalculates. But `useMemo` compares using `Object.is`. For objects, `Object.is` checks reference equality. So if the provider creates `{ lang, t }` each render, it's a new reference, and `useMemo` recalculates.

I'm not reproducing the issue. Let me check if maybe the issue is related to the specific version change. Let me look at the `npm` published versions to see if there's a diff.

Actually, let me look more carefully at the source code. Perhaps the issue is in the `I18nProvider` where it uses `useTranslation()` to get `parentLang`:

```tsx
const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
```

The `useTranslation` calls `useContext(I18nContext)` which gets the value from the nearest `I18nContext.Provider`. If the component using `I18nProvider` is not wrapped in another `I18nProvider`, it gets the default context value:

```tsx
context = React.createContext<I18n>({
  t: (k) => (Array.isArray(k) ? k[0] : k),
  lang: '',
})
```

This default value is a STABLE object that never changes. Now, `useTranslation` wraps this in `useMemo`:

```tsx
return useMemo(
  () => ({
    ...ctx,
    t: wrapTWithDefaultNs(ctx.t, defaultNS),
  }),
  [ctx, defaultNS]
)
```

Since `ctx` (the default context value) is stable, and `defaultNS` is `undefined`, the `useMemo` returns the same reference every time. That's fine.

But what if there IS a parent `I18nProvider`? Then `ctx` comes from that parent's value, which changes each time the parent renders. So `useMemo` recalculates. Also fine.

Hmm, let me look at the transpiled code to see if there's a difference. Let me compare the source `useTranslation.tsx` with the built `lib/esm/useTranslation.js`:

Source:
```tsx
function useTranslationInPages(defaultNS?: string): I18n {
  const ctx = useContext(I18nContext)
  return useMemo(
    () => ({
      ...ctx,
      t: wrapTWithDefaultNs(ctx.t, defaultNS),
    }),
    [ctx, defaultNS]
  )
}
```

Built:
```js
function useTranslationInPages(defaultNS) {
    var ctx = useContext(I18nContext);
    return useMemo(function () { return (__assign(__assign({}, ctx), { t: wrapTWithDefaultNs(ctx.t, defaultNS) })); }, [ctx, defaultNS]);
}
```

They match. The built code is correct.

The effect depends on `namespaces.join()`. If `namespaces` is `['common']`, `namespaces.join()` is `'common'`. This doesn't change when `lang` changes. Look at `I18nProvider.tsx`:

```tsx
export default function I18nProvider({
  lang: lng,
  namespaces = {},
  children,
  config: newConfig = {},
}: I18nProviderProps) {
  const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
  ...
```

And `useTranslation.tsx`:

```tsx
export default function useTranslation(defaultNS?: string): I18n {
  const appDir = globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__
  const useT = appDir?.config ? createTranslation : useTranslationInPages
  return useT(defaultNS)
}
```

If `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set (which it is in Next.js pages router via `appWithI18n`), then `appDir?.config` would be truthy, and it would use `createTranslation` instead of `useTranslationInPages`!

Let me check `appWithI18n`:

```tsx
if (lang && namespaces) {
  globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__ = { lang, namespaces, config }
}
```

Yes! `appWithI18n` sets `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` to `{ lang, namespaces, config }`. And `useTranslation` checks for `appDir?.config`. If `config` is truthy (which it is), it uses `createTranslation`!

Now let's look at `createTranslation`:

```tsx
export default function createTranslation(defaultNS?: string) {
  const { lang, namespaces, config } = globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__ ?? {}
  const localesToIgnore = config.localesToIgnore || ['default']
  const ignoreLang = !lang || localesToIgnore.includes(lang)
  const getT = () => {
    const t = transCore({
      config,
      allNamespaces: namespaces,
      pluralRules: new Intl.PluralRules(ignoreLang ? undefined : lang),
      lang,
    })

    return wrapTWithDefaultNs(t, defaultNS)
  }

  const t = isServer() ? getT() : useMemo(getT, [defaultNS, lang])
  return { t, lang }
}
```

This reads `lang` from `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`, NOT from the React context! So if `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set, the `I18nProvider` is completely bypassed for `useTranslation` calls!

Wait, but this is the app directory path. Let me check the condition again:

```tsx
const appDir = globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__
const useT = appDir?.config ? createTranslation : useTranslationInPages
```

If `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` has a `config` property, it uses `createTranslation`. But `appWithI18n` sets `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__ = { lang, namespaces, config }` where `config` is the full config object. So yes, `appDir?.config` would be truthy, and `useTranslation` would use `createTranslation` which reads from the global, not from React context!

But wait, `appWithI18n` is the HOC for the pages directory. The `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is supposed to be for the app directory, not the pages directory. But the code in `appWithI18n` sets it unconditionally!

Actually, let me look at this more carefully. The comment in `createTranslation` says "Only for App directory". But `appWithI18n` (which is for pages directory) sets `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`. So `useTranslation` would use `createTranslation` in pages directory too!

That's the bug! When `appWithI18n` sets `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`, the `useTranslation` hook switches to using `createTranslation` which reads from the global variable rather than from React context. The global variable is set once during `getInitialProps` and never updated when the language changes at runtime.

But wait, let me check the actual `appWithI18n` code:

```tsx
function AppWithTranslations(props: Props) {

  const lang = props.pageProps?.__lang || props.__lang || defaultLocale
  const namespaces = props.pageProps?.__namespaces || props.__namespaces

  if (lang && namespaces) {
    globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__ = { lang, namespaces, config }
  }

  return (
    <I18nProvider lang={lang} namespaces={namespaces} config={config}>
      <AppToTranslate {...props} />
    </I18nProvider>
  )
}
```

Yes, this sets `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` to the initial `lang` from props. Then when the user changes the language via `I18nProvider`, the `useTranslation` hook would still read from `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` which has the old `lang` value!

Now let me look at how the plugin sets things up. But we don't have the plugin code here.

Let me think about this differently. Let me search for any recent changes by looking at the code patterns more carefully.

Actually, I just realized something important. Let me look at the `I18nProvider` again:

```tsx
const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
```

And `useTranslation`:

```tsx
export default function useTranslation(defaultNS?: string): I18n {
  const appDir = globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__
  const useT = appDir?.config ? createTranslation : useTranslationInPages
  return useT(defaultNS)
}
```

Now, `createTranslation`:

```tsx
export default function createTranslation(defaultNS?: string) {
  const { lang, namespaces, config } = globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__ ?? {}
  ...
}
```

If `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set by the plugin (or by `appWithI18n`), then `useTranslation` will use `createTranslation` which ignores React context entirely! 

But wait, the PR says this worked in 3.0.0. So maybe in 3.0.0, `useTranslation` didn't have this branching logic? Or maybe `appWithI18n` didn't set `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`?

Actually, looking at the code again, I think the issue might be different. Let me check if there's a problem with the `I18nProvider` itself when `useTranslation` is called within it.

Look at `I18nProvider.tsx` line 16:

```tsx
const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
```

If `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set, `useTranslation` calls `createTranslation` which reads `lang` from `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`. This `lang` is the initial server-side language, not the one from the parent React context.

But this is only relevant if there's a PARENT `I18nProvider`. In the user's case, they have:

```tsx
<I18nProvider key={lang} lang={lang}>
```

This is the top-level provider. So `parentLang` from `useTranslation()` would be either from the default context (if `useTranslationInPages` is used) or from `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` (if `createTranslation` is used). In either case, `lng` (which is the prop) takes precedence, so `parentLang` doesn't matter.

But what about the INNER components? They call `useTranslation()` and if `createTranslation` is used, they'd read from `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` which has the OLD language!

Wait, let me check: does the `I18nProvider` update `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` when the language changes? NO! It only updates React context. So if `createTranslation` is being used (which reads from global), the language change in `I18nProvider` would be ignored!

Let me verify this hypothesis by looking at the test file for `useTranslation`

So the tests for `createTranslation` (app-dir path) set `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` with `config: {}` (empty object). 

Now let me understand the condition better. In `useTranslation`:

```tsx
const appDir = globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__
const useT = appDir?.config ? createTranslation : useTranslationInPages
```

If `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set (by plugin or `appWithI18n`), AND it has a truthy `config`, it uses `createTranslation`. Otherwise it uses `useTranslationInPages`.

Now, let me check if `appWithI18n` is supposed to be used with pages directory. Looking at its code:

```tsx
export default function appWithI18n(
  AppToTranslate: NextComponentType,
  config: LoaderConfig = {}
) {
  if (!config.isLoader && config.loader !== false) {
    console.warn(
      '🚨 [next-translate] You can remove the "appWithI18n" HoC on the _app.js, unless you set "loader: false" in your i18n config file.'
    )
  }
```

The warning says you can REMOVE `appWithI18n` unless you set `loader: false`. So in normal usage with the plugin, `appWithI18n` should NOT be used. The plugin handles everything.

But wait, `appWithI18n` sets `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`. If the plugin also sets it, then... Let me check if the plugin sets `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` or not.

Let me take a different approach. Let me look at the code and think about what bug would cause `lang` to be ignored.

Actually, I just realized something. Let me look at `useTranslation` again:

```tsx
export default function useTranslation(defaultNS?: string): I18n {
  const appDir = globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__
  const useT = appDir?.config ? createTranslation : useTranslationInPages
  return useT(defaultNS)
}
```

The condition `appDir?.config` - if `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is `undefined`, `appDir` is `undefined`, and `appDir?.config` is `undefined` (falsy), so it uses `useTranslationInPages`. That's the pages router path.

If `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set with a config, it uses `createTranslation`. That's the app directory path.

Now, the PR says `I18nProvider` ignores `lang`. If the user is using pages directory (which they are, they mention `next-translate-plugin`), then `useTranslation` should use `useTranslationInPages`. Unless the plugin sets `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`, which would cause `createTranslation` to be used instead.

But wait, if `createTranslation` is used, then `I18nProvider`'s lang would be ignored because `createTranslation` reads from `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`, not from React context.

So maybe the bug is that `useTranslation` should check more carefully whether we're in app directory or pages directory. Currently it just checks for the existence of `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` with a config, but maybe the plugin also sets this, causing the wrong path to be taken.

But actually, the PR says this worked in 3.0.0. So something must have changed. Let me check if the `createTranslation` function was added in 3.0.1 or 3.0.2.

Since we only have the current code, let me look at the structure to understand the expected behavior. The issue mentions `next-translate` 3.0.2 and `next-translate-plugin` 2.6.2. 

Let me look at if there's an issue with how `I18nProvider` passes config to the internal context:

```tsx
return (
  <I18nContext.Provider value={{ lang, t }}>
    <InternalContext.Provider value={{ ns: allNamespaces, config }}>
      {children}
    </InternalContext.Provider>
  </I18nContext.Provider>
)
```

And `useTranslation` in pages mode:

```tsx
function useTranslationInPages(defaultNS?: string): I18n {
  const ctx = useContext(I18nContext)
  return useMemo(
    () => ({
      ...ctx,
      t: wrapTWithDefaultNs(ctx.t, defaultNS),
    }),
    [ctx, defaultNS]
  )
}
```

This reads from `I18nContext`. The `I18nProvider` provides both `I18nContext` (with `{ lang, t }`) and `InternalContext` (with `{ ns, config }`).

Now, what if the issue is that `useTranslation`'s `useMemo` has a bug? Let me check:

```tsx
return useMemo(
  () => ({
    ...ctx,
    t: wrapTWithDefaultNs(ctx.t, defaultNS),
  }),
  [ctx, defaultNS]
)
```

`ctx` is `{ lang, t }`. When the provider updates with a new `lang`, it creates a new `{ lang, t }` object. So `ctx` is a new reference. The `useMemo` should recalculate.

But what if `wrapTWithDefaultNs` returns the same `t` function when `defaultNS` is undefined? Let me check:

```tsx
export default function wrapTWithDefaultNs(
  oldT: Translate,
  ns?: string
): Translate {
  if (typeof ns !== 'string') return oldT

  // Use default namespace if namespace is missing
  const t: Translate = (key, query, options) => {
    return oldT(key, query, { ns, ...options })
  }

  return t
}
```

If `ns` is not a string (undefined), it returns `oldT` directly. So the `t` in `useMemo`'s return value is the same reference as `ctx.t`. So the returned object from `useMemo` has the same `t` reference but a new `lang` string. This is still a new object, so child components using `useTranslation` would get a new `ctx` reference.

Unless... the issue is that `useMemo` does a shallow comparison and since `lang` might be the same... No, `useMemo` uses `Object.is` (reference equality) on each dependency. `ctx` is a new object each time, so it should update.

cd /testbed && cat > __tests__/repro3.test.js << 'EOF'
import React, { useState, useMemo } from 'react'
import { render, cleanup, act } from '@testing-library/react'
import I18nProvider from '../src/I18nProvider'
import useTranslation from '../src/useTranslation'

describe('I18nProvider dynamic lang change', () => {
  afterEach(cleanup)

  test('lang change re-renders children with new lang', () => {
    let setLang
    
    const Inner = () => {
      const { t, lang } = useTranslation()
      return <div data-testid="inner">{lang}:{t('common:hello')}</div>
    }

    const App = () => {
      const [lang, _setLang] = useState('en')
      setLang = _setLang
      return (
        <I18nProvider lang={lang} namespaces={{
          common: { hello: lang === 'en' ? 'Hello' : 'Hola' },
        }}>
          <Inner />
        </I18nProvider>
      )
    }

    const { container } = render(<App />)
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('en:Hello')
    
    // Change language via state update
    act(() => setLang('es'))
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('es:Hola')
  })
  
  test('lang change with useTranslation without defaultNS', () => {
    let setLang
    
    const Inner = () => {
      const { t, lang } = useTranslation()
      const result = t('common:hello')
      return <div data-testid="inner">{lang}:{result}</div>
    }

    const namespaces = {
      common: { hello_en: 'Hello', hello_es: 'Hola' },
    }
    const langMap = { en: 'Hello', es: 'Hola' }
    
    const App = () => {
      const [lang, _setLang] = useState('en')
      setLang = _setLang
      return (
        <I18nProvider lang={lang} namespaces={{
          common: { hello: langMap[lang] },
        }}>
          <Inner />
        </I18nProvider>
      )
    }

    const { container } = render(<App />)
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('en:Hello')
    
    act(() => setLang('es'))
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('es:Hola')
  })
  
  test('nested I18nProvider with lang change', () => {
    let setLang
    
    const Inner = () => {
      const { t, lang } = useTranslation()
      return <div data-testid="inner">{lang}:{t('common:hello')}</div>
    }
    
    const InnerProvider = ({ children }) => {
      const { lang } = useTranslation()
      return (
        <I18nProvider lang={lang} namespaces={{
          common: { hello: lang === 'en' ? 'Hello' : 'Hola' },
        }}>
          {children}
        </I18nProvider>
      )
    }

    const App = () => {
      const [lang, _setLang] = useState('en')
      setLang = _setLang
      return (
        <I18nProvider lang={lang} namespaces={{}}>
          <InnerProvider>
            <Inner />
          </InnerProvider>
        </I18nProvider>
      )
    }

    const { container } = render(<App />)
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('en:Hello')
    
    act(() => setLang('es'))
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('es:Hola')
  })
  
  test('simulate PR exact scenario', () => {
    let setLang
    
    const Inner = () => {
      const { t, lang } = useTranslation('common')
      return <div data-testid="inner">{lang}:{t('languageName')}</div>
    }
    
    const DynamicNamespaces = ({ namespaces, children }) => {
      const { lang } = useTranslation()
      const [loaded, setLoaded] = React.useState(false)
      const [pageNs, setPageNs] = React.useState([])
      
      React.useEffect(() => {
        // Simulate loading translations
        const nsData = {
          en: { common: { languageName: 'English' } },
          es: { common: { languageName: 'Español' } },
          fr: { common: { languageName: 'Français' } },
        }
        const loadedNs = namespaces.map(ns => nsData[lang]?.[ns] || {})
        setPageNs(loadedNs)
        setLoaded(true)
      }, [lang, namespaces.join()])
      
      if (!loaded) return null
      
      return (
        <I18nProvider
          lang={lang}
          namespaces={namespaces.reduce((obj, ns, i) => {
            obj[ns] = pageNs[i]
            return obj
          }, {})}
        >
          {children}
        </I18nProvider>
      )
    }

    const App = () => {
      const [lang, _setLang] = useState('en')
      setLang = _setLang
      return (
        <I18nProvider key={lang} lang={lang}>
          <DynamicNamespaces namespaces={['common']}>
            <Inner />
          </DynamicNamespaces>
        </I18nProvider>
      )
    }

    const { container } = render(<App />)
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('en:English')
    
    act(() => setLang('es'))
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('es:Español')
    
    act(() => setLang('fr'))
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('fr:Français')
  })
})

import React, { useState } from 'react'
import { render, cleanup, act } from '@testing-library/react'
import I18nProvider from '../src/I18nProvider'
import useTranslation from '../src/useTranslation'

describe('I18nProvider with globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__', () => {
  afterEach(cleanup)
  
  afterEach(() => {
    delete globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__
  })

  test('lang change when globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__ is set (simulating appWithI18n)', () => {
    // Simulate what appWithI18n does: set globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__
    globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__ = {
      lang: 'en',
      namespaces: { common: { hello: 'Hello' } },
      config: { defaultLocale: 'en' },
    }
    
    let setLang
    
    const Inner = () => {
      const { t, lang } = useTranslation()
      return <div data-testid="inner">{lang}:{t('common:hello')}</div>
    }

    const App = () => {
      const [lang, _setLang] = useState('en')
      setLang = _setLang
      return (
        <I18nProvider lang={lang} namespaces={{
          common: { hello: lang === 'en' ? 'Hello' : 'Hola' },
        }}>
          <Inner />
        </I18nProvider>
      )
    }

    const { container } = render(<App />)
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('en:Hello')
    
    act(() => setLang('es'))
    // This should show 'es:Hola' but if createTranslation is used,
    // it might show 'en:Hello' (because globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__.lang is still 'en')
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('es:Hola')
  })
  
  test('lang change when globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__ has empty config', () => {
    globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__ = {
      lang: 'en',
      namespaces: { common: { hello: 'Hello' } },
      config: {}, // empty object
    }
    
    let setLang
    
    const Inner = () => {
      const { t, lang } = useTranslation()
      return <div data-testid="inner">{lang}:{t('common:hello')}</div>
    }

      const [lang, _setLang] = useState('en')
      setLang = _setLang
      return (
        <I18nProvider lang={lang} namespaces={{
          common: { hello: lang === 'en' ? 'Hello' : 'Hola' },
        }}>
          <Inner />
        </I18nProvider>
      )
    }

    const { container } = render(<App />)
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('en:Hello')
    
    act(() => setLang('es'))
    expect(container.textContent).toContain('es:Hola')
  })
})

2026-05-30 07:54:58,785 - INFO - swea-agent-aralroca__next-translate-1259 - 💭 THOUGHT
Bingo! I found the bug! 

When `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set (with ANY config, even empty), the `useTranslation` function uses `createTranslation` instead of `useTranslationInPages`. And `createTranslation` reads `lang` from `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`, which is never updated by `I18nProvider`. So the language change is completely ignored!

Now let me understand the condition:

```tsx
const useT = appDir?.config ? createTranslation : useTranslationInPages
```

The issue is that `appDir?.config` is truthy even when `config` is an empty object `{}`. The condition should check if we're actually in the app directory, not just if `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` has a config property.

But wait, there's another issue. Even with a non-empty config, the `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set by `appWithI18n` for pages directory too:

```tsx
if (lang && namespaces) {
  globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__ = { lang, namespaces, config }
}
```

So when using `appWithI18n` (which is for pages directory), `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` gets set, and then `useTranslation` incorrectly uses `createTranslation` which bypasses React context.

But the PR description says this worked in 3.0.0. So maybe `appWithI18n` didn't set `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` in 3.0.0? Or maybe the condition in `useTranslation` was different?

Let me also check the test for app-dir: the test sets `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` with `config: {}` (empty object). The condition `appDir?.config` would be truthy for `{}`. So even the existing test uses `createTranslation` successfully because it doesn't test dynamic language changes.

Now let me understand the full impact. The `useTranslation` function is used by:
1. `I18nProvider` (to get parentLang)
2. `DynamicNamespaces` (to get current lang)
3. User components (to translate)

If `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set, ALL of these use `createTranslation` which reads from the global, not from React context. So `I18nProvider`'s lang prop is effectively ignored.

Now, how should this be fixed? 

Option 1: Make `I18nProvider` update `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` when lang changes.

Option 2: Change the condition in `useTranslation` to properly detect pages vs app directory.

Option 3: Make `useTranslation` check both the global and React context.

I think the proper fix is to make `I18nProvider` update `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` when it renders, so that the global stays in sync with the React context. This way, both app directory and pages directory benefit from the update.

But actually, `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is also used by `createTranslation` for the app directory. In the app directory, there is no React context (server components can't use context). So the global is the source of truth for app directory.

For pages directory, the React context should be the source of truth. But `useTranslation` currently prefers the global over context.

I think the right fix is: `I18nProvider` should update `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` when it renders. This ensures that both the global and the React context are in sync.

Let me verify this and implement the fix:



🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/src/I18nProvider.tsx   --old_str 'import React, { createContext, useContext } from '"'"'react'"'"'
import { useRouter } from '"'"'next/router'"'"'
import I18nContext from '"'"'./context'"'"'
import transCore from '"'"'./transCore'"'"'
import useTranslation from '"'"'./useTranslation'"'"'
import { I18nDictionary, I18nProviderProps } from '"'"'.'"'"'

export const InternalContext = createContext({ ns: {}, config: {} })

export default function I18nProvider({
  lang: lng,
  namespaces = {},
  children,
  config: newConfig = {},
}: I18nProviderProps) {
  const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
  const { locale, defaultLocale } = useRouter() || {}
  const internal = useContext(InternalContext)
  const allNamespaces: Record<string, I18nDictionary> = {
    ...initialBrowserNamespaces(),
    ...internal.ns,
    ...namespaces,
  }
  const lang = lng || parentLang || locale || defaultLocale || '"'"''"'"'
  const config = { ...internal.config, ...newConfig }
  const localesToIgnore = config.localesToIgnore || ['"'"'default'"'"']
  const ignoreLang = !lang || localesToIgnore.includes(lang)
  const pluralRules = new Intl.PluralRules(ignoreLang ? undefined : lang)
  const t = transCore({ config, allNamespaces, pluralRules, lang })

  return (
    <I18nContext.Provider value={{ lang, t }}>
      <InternalContext.Provider value={{ ns: allNamespaces, config }}>
        {children}
      </InternalContext.Provider>
    </I18nContext.Provider>
  )
}' --new_str 'import React, { createContext, useContext } from '"'"'react'"'"'
import { useRouter } from '"'"'next/router'"'"'
import I18nContext from '"'"'./context'"'"'
import transCore from '"'"'./transCore'"'"'
import useTranslation from '"'"'./useTranslation'"'"'
import { I18nDictionary, I18nProviderProps } from '"'"'.'"'"'

export const InternalContext = createContext({ ns: {}, config: {} })

export default function I18nProvider({
  lang: lng,
  namespaces = {},
  children,
  config: newConfig = {},
}: I18nProviderProps) {
  const { lang: parentLang } = useTranslation()
  const { locale, defaultLocale } = useRouter() || {}
  const internal = useContext(InternalContext)
  const allNamespaces: Record<string, I18nDictionary> = {
    ...initialBrowserNamespaces(),
    ...internal.ns,
    ...namespaces,
  }
  const lang = lng || parentLang || locale || defaultLocale || '"'"''"'"'
  const config = { ...internal.config, ...newConfig }
  const localesToIgnore = config.localesToIgnore || ['"'"'default'"'"']
  const ignoreLang = !lang || localesToIgnore.includes(lang)
  const pluralRules = new Intl.PluralRules(ignoreLang ? undefined : lang)
  const t = transCore({ config, allNamespaces, pluralRules, lang })

  // Update globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__ to keep it in sync with React context
  // This is necessary for components that use createTranslation (app directory path)
  // which reads from globalThis instead of React context
  if (typeof window !== '"'"'undefined'"'"' && globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__?.config) {
    globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__.lang = lang
    globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__.namespaces = allNamespaces
  }

  return (
    <I18nContext.Provider value={{ lang, t }}>
      <InternalContext.Provider value={{ ns: allNamespaces, config }}>

When `DynamicNamespaces` loads new namespaces after a language change, it renders a new `I18nProvider`. The `I18nProvider` in `DynamicNamespaces` will also update `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` when it renders. This is fine.\n\n2. **What if there are multiple nested `I18nProvider`s?** Each one updates `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` with its own `lang` and `allNamespaces`. The innermost one\'s values will "win" because they are set last during rendering. This is correct - the innermost provider should have the most accurate state.\n\n3. **What about server-side rendering?** On the server, `typeof window === \'undefined\'`, so we skip the update. This is correct because on the server, React context works normally and `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is not used for translation (the pages router uses props, and the app directory uses the global directly without `I18nProvider`).\n\n4. **What if `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` doesn\'t have a `config` property?** The condition `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__?.config` ensures we only update when the global is being used for app directory translations. If `config` is not set, `useTranslation` uses `useTranslationInPages` (React context), so we don\'t need to update the global.\n\nBut wait, I should also consider the case where `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set WITHOUT a config (or with a falsy config). In that case, `useTranslation` uses `useTranslationInPages`. But what if later, `I18nProvider` sets `config` on `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`? All 144 tests pass.

Now let me think about edge cases and whether my fix is complete:

1. **What about the `DynamicNamespaces` component?** It also creates an `I18nProvider`. When `DynamicNamespaces` loads new namespaces after a language change, it renders a new `I18nProvider`. The `I18nProvider` in `DynamicNamespaces` will also update `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` when it renders. This is fine.

2. **What if there are multiple nested `I18nProvider`s?** Each one updates `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` with its own `lang` and `allNamespaces`. The innermost one's values will "win" because they are set last during rendering. This is correct - the innermost provider should have the most accurate state.

3. **What about server-side rendering?** On the server, `typeof window === 'undefined'`, so we skip the update. This is correct because on the server, React context works normally and `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is not used for translation (the pages router uses props, and the app directory uses the global directly without `I18nProvider`).

4. **What if `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` doesn't have a `config` property?** The condition `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__?.config` ensures we only update when the global is being used for app directory translations. If `config` is not set, `useTranslation` uses `useTranslationInPages` (React context), so we don't need to update the global.

But wait, I should also consider the case where `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set WITHOUT a config (or with a falsy config). In that case, `useTranslation` uses `useTranslationInPages`. But what if later, `I18nProvider` sets `config` on `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`? That could cause a switch from `useTranslationInPages` to `createTranslation`.

Actually, my fix doesn't set `config` on `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` - it only updates `lang` and `namespaces`. The `config` is set by `appWithI18n` or the plugin initially. So the condition in `useTranslation` (`appDir?.config`) would already be true before `I18nProvider` renders. My fix just keeps `lang` and `namespaces` in sync.

Let me also consider: what if the user is using the pages directory without `appWithI18n` and without the plugin setting `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`? Then `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` would be undefined, and `useTranslation` would use `useTranslationInPages`. My fix's condition `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__?.config` would be undefined, so we skip the update. This is correct.

I think the fix is solid. But let me also double-check by looking at the `DynamicNamespaces` component - it also has `useTranslation` which could be affected:

```tsx
export default function DynamicNamespaces({
  dynamic,
  namespaces = [],
  fallback,
  children,
}: DynamicNamespacesProps): any {
  const config = useContext(InternalContext).config as I18nConfig
  const { lang } = useTranslation()
  ...
```

If `useTranslation` uses `createTranslation` (because `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` is set), then `lang` comes from the global. With my fix, `I18nProvider` updates the global, so `DynamicNamespaces` will get the correct `lang` from `useTranslation`.

But there's another subtle issue: `DynamicNamespaces` has a `useEffect` that depends on `[namespaces.join()]`. When `lang` changes but `namespaces` stays the same, the effect doesn't re-run. So if `DynamicNamespaces` is NOT remounted (no `key={lang}` on parent), the namespaces won't be reloaded.

However, the PR description shows the user using `key={lang}` on the outer `I18nProvider`, which forces remount of everything. So that's fine.

But what about users who don't use `key={lang}`? They would still have the issue that `DynamicNamespaces` doesn't reload namespaces when language changes. But that's a separate issue from the one described in the PR (the PR says `I18nProvider` ignores `lang` entirely).

Let me verify that my fix addresses the exact scenario from the PR:

1. User sets `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` (via plugin or `appWithI18n`)
2. User renders `<I18nProvider key={lang} lang={lang}>`
3. `I18nProvider` mounts with new `lang`
4. `I18nProvider` calls `useTranslation()` which (due to `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` being set) uses `createTranslation`, getting `lang` from `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`
5. But `lng` prop takes precedence: `const lang = lng || parentLang || ...`
6. `I18nProvider` updates `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__.lang = lang`
7. Children call `useTranslation()` which uses `createTranslation`, getting the updated `lang` from `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__`

This works! The key insight is that `I18nProvider` itself uses `lng` (the prop) for its own `lang` variable (because `lng || parentLang` and `lng` is truthy), but children use `createTranslation` which reads from the global. By updating the global, children see the correct language.

Let me now also think about an alternative approach: instead of updating `globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__` in `I18nProvider`, we could change the condition in `useTranslation` to not use `createTranslation` when we're in pages directory. But determining whether we're in pages or app directory is not straightforward.

Another alternative: we could change `useTranslation` to check both the global and React context, preferring the context if available. But that would be a more invasive change.

I think my current fix is the minimal and correct approach. Let me verify the final state of all modified files:

But typically, for app directory, you'd use `AppDirI18nProvider` and for pages directory, you'd use `I18nProvider`. The fix ensures that `I18nProvider` keeps the global in sync if it was set.

Now let me also consider if the `DynamicNamespaces` component's `useEffect` should also depend on `lang`:

```tsx
useEffect(() => {
  loadNamespaces()
}, [namespaces.join()])
```

This only depends on `namespaces.join()`, not on `lang`. So if `lang` changes but `namespaces` stays the same, the effect doesn't re-run. This could be another bug, but it's separate from the PR description. The PR description says the user uses `key={lang}` which forces remount, so the effect runs on mount anyway.

However, I should note that this could be an additional issue for users who don't use `key={lang}`. But the PR specifically says `I18nProvider` ignores `lang`, which my fix addresses.

2026-05-30 07:57:53,903 - DEBUG - swea-tools-aralroca__next-translate-1259 - Retrieved state from environment: {'working_dir': '/testbed'}
2026-05-30 07:57:53,909 - INFO - swea-agent-aralroca__next-translate-1259 - 🤖 MODEL INPUT
OBSERVATION:

import getConfig from './getConfig'
import transCore from './transCore'
import wrapTWithDefaultNs from './wrapTWithDefaultNs'
import { I18nDictionary, LocaleLoader } from './index'

export default async function getT(
  locale = '',
  namespace: string | string[] = ''
) {
  const appDir = globalThis.__NEXT_TRANSLATE__
  const config = appDir?.config ?? getConfig()
  const defaultLoader = async () => Promise.resolve<I18nDictionary>({})
  const lang = locale || config.defaultLocale || ''
  const loader: LocaleLoader = config.loadLocaleFrom || defaultLoader

  const namespaces = Array.isArray(namespace) ? namespace : [namespace]

  const allNamespaces: Record<string, I18nDictionary> = {}
  await Promise.all(
    namespaces.map(async (namespace) => {
      allNamespaces[namespace] = await loader(lang, namespace)
    })
  )

  const localesToIgnore = config.localesToIgnore || ['default']
  const ignoreLang = localesToIgnore.includes(lang)
  const pluralRules = new Intl.PluralRules(ignoreLang ? undefined : lang)
  const t = transCore({ config, allNamespaces, pluralRules, lang })

  const defaultNamespace = namespaces[0]
  return wrapTWithDefaultNs(t, defaultNamespace)
}
